
   Message Format
  ----------------

   Message #1 of 8283 <"- ASCII Signiture Rebuilt"|"- ASCII Signiture As-Is">*

   <Subject>

   <1 blank separator line>

   <Date/Time>

   <Person & email address>

   <2 blank separator lines then...>

   <Message - "As-Is">

   <2 blank lines then @'s as divider line>


   * ASCII signitures have been rebuilt where possible.
     Unfortunately Yahoo store messages in a way which means more than 1 space
     is stored as just 1 space. Viewing the message source, and then trying to
     view HTML source in Firefox didn't make any difference.
     Where I have been unable to rebuild the ASCII signitures I have simply put
     "ASCII Signiture As-Is" by the message number.

     Thanks to Mark de Jong (from the AMOS-LIST) for helping me with rebuilding
     Floquet's ASCII signiture. (who else would keep emails for 7 years?!)

     Thanks to Andrew Allen for preserving Peter Cahill's ASCII signiture for
     me (see message 1613) in November 1998.

     Thanks to Michael Cox, as I was able to cross-reference some emails from
     the Onelist archives with ones posted to the Yahoo one to reinstate email
     addresses that Yahoo has discarded, and rebuild some ASCII signitures.


   Message From Archivist
  ------------------------

   I hope everyone enjoys reading the messages and appreciates me archiving
   them. It took hours of work to get all the info into this file and then
   rebuild the ASCII signitures as best as I could.
   Don't forget to join, or atleast visit, the Y! AMOS-LIST group:

     http://groups.yahoo.com/group/amos-list

Re: Re: Data Statements

Tue Nov 2, 1999 11:16 am
"floquet" <floquet@hp-sc.univ-lille2.fr>


Truls Osmundsen wrote:
> From: Truls Osmundsen <ozzy1@online.no>
> * Svar til:* /Andrew Crowe/ (#andrewcrowe@enterprise.net#)
> * Dato var:* /29-Oct-99/
> * Emne var:* /[amos-list] Re: Data Statements/
> > It takes a long time to read data statements? What amiga are you
> > using?!? ;)
> If one got sooo many statements, why not just create a screen with
> a progress bar with the words "Please wait" ?
> It can be done in a proffesional way, keeping the user from saying "crap".
> :)

After thinking about this problem, turning it up 'n down, I agree with
you, Truls,
it is the best way.
Even storing all datas in a bank, and poking at varptr(x)+I won't be
faster, and may cause crashes...
I just think about this : Maybe you can try to use the hard-pain way:
a$(1,1)="1st value"
a$(1,2)="2nd value"
...and 585463 lines later:
a$(127,16)="Last value (phew!)"

If you write a little prog that generates a .ASC file containing all the
variables, the you just have to merge this into your project... I really
don't know if this will speed up the intitializations. Maybe...

Naaaaah, progress bar rulez !

	Message #4363 of 8282 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Off-Topic: Scsi.device

Tue Nov 2, 1999 12:17 pm
Rune Keller <keller@vip.cybercity.dk>


Sorry to bother you with off-topic stuff, but I have a problem I can't seem to
solve.

At exactly 1st november 00:00 I started to get two nasty guru-style requestors
every time I boot. They say something like:

"OS Development Group Warning

You are using an expired beta of
IDE_scsidsk 43.24 (9.11.98)

For legal and safety reasons please replace it."

The other requestor says the same, except that file is "fs 43.20 (9.11.98)"

It seems that it is the files Loadv43Module, a1000.ld.strip and fastfilesystem
that causes the mess. These come from the Amiga.de page and are supposed to
fix scsi.device for the problems with the 4Gb limit on harddisks and have
worked fine until now...

Anyway, the betas are now expired and there are apparently no new versions
anywhere. I can set my clock a year back, but that's not really a great
solution.

Have anybody experienced the same (somebody must have!) or do anybody know a
good solution?

--
rune j. keller - sporuplundsvej 105 - dk-8472 sporup - keller@vip.cybercity.dk
- i got a bad feeling about this one  - when did you feel good about anything?

	Message #4368 of 8282

Amos to C converter

Tue Nov 2, 1999 3:14 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>I`ve been thinking about making an Amos source code to C source code
>converter so that I can recompile all my Amos stuff on the PC...
>Does anyone fancy giving me a hand re-writing the 400+ Amos commands as a
>vast pile of header files in C?

This is a cool idea but completely unnecessary unless you simply want the
fun of the project itself.

If you are familiar with C/C++ then simply download the Allegro library
and you will find all of the audio/video commands which AMOS has
plus a bunch more offering realtime rotation, scaling, and even true 3d.

Have fun!

	Message #4373 of 8282

Location of Allegro: A Powerful, FREE C/C++ Gam Programming Library

Tue Nov 2, 1999 6:58 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


GB> If you are familiar with C/C++ then simply download the Allegro library
GB> and you will find all of the audio/video commands which AMOS has
GB> plus a bunch more offering realtime rotation, scaling, and even true
GB> 3d.

GD> Woah! where do I get it?

Here is the URL which I have encrypted with a quick & easy
C program I just threw together. I truly am too kind. lol! :)

URL: IVWT?56_`a9`NZd\R@WYbeeF\iIqhM`LMgjvt/

Here is the key part of the encryption:
*StringChar++ = ( toupper( *StringChar ) + position );

Where position is the current character position in the URL string
and the first character (the "I") is position number 1.

Very easy to decode. Most likely, someone is already writing a
simple AMOS program to decode it.

Solve the riddle, decode the URL and find Allegro!! :-)

	Message #4377 of 8282

Key to the riddle!!

Tue Nov 2, 1999 10:15 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


GB> .... and StringChar is obviously(??) the name of the variable holding
GB> the original URL and is also (obviously) being used to hold the
GB> encoded string.

Okay, here is the single line which when placed inside a loop the length
of the encrypted string will decode the encrypted URL:
*StringChar++ -= position;

Obviously that C speak basically translates to the following
AMOS speak:
Mid$(STRINGCHAR$, POSITION, 1) =
Chr$( Asc( Mid$(STRINGCHAR$, POSITION, 1) ) - POSITION )
OR:
CHAR = Asc( Mid$(STRINGCHAR$, POSITION, 1) ) - POSITION
Mid$(STRINGCHAR$, POSITION, 1) = Chr$( CHAR )


Have fun!!

Re: Re: Riddle for you

Tue Nov 2, 1999 9:40 pm
Claude Heiland-allen <claude.heiland-allen@lincoln.oxford.ac.uk>


> GB> Here is the key part of the encryption:
> GB> *StringChar++ = ( toupper( *StringChar ) + position );
> GB> Where position is the current character position in the URL string
> GB> and the first character (the "I") is position number 1.
>
> .... and StringChar is obviously(??) the name of the variable holding the
> original URL and is also (obviously) being used to hold the encoded
> string.

Erm, I'm no C expert but surely the above code is not legal? The C standard
doesn't say when the ++ happens, I assume you want it to happen after the
entire line and not inbetween accesses to *StringChar.


Feeling particularly pedantic this evening.

actually, knowing from experience, its not the cpu speed on the amiga that
slows things down, its the blitter/graphics transfer bandwidth. Hence,
things run at the same speed on an A1200/020 as with 060. True, they don't
need compiling... Anything that uses low computational power will be slowed
down by the gfx bandwidth. Have a look at any proggie that uses a lot of
graphics updating.

Re: Riddle for you

Wed Nov 3, 1999 12:36 am
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


GB> *StringChar++ = ( toupper( *StringChar ) + position );
CH> Erm, I'm no C expert but surely the above code is not legal?
CH> The C standard doesn't say when the ++ happens, I assume
CH> you want it to happen after the entire line and not inbetween
CH> accesses to *StringChar.

Of course it is legal.
If it had not been I would not have wrote it. lol ;-)
.
I am post-incrementing. I know exactly when the increment occurs.
After the entire line is processed and the new value has been
loaded into StringChar.
If you wanted to increment it before the value was pulled from
the variable you would use pre-increment ( ie. *++StringChar ).

This is of course off topic and I know the elders will surely make
noise soon.

Re: AMOS Code Key to the riddle!!

Wed Nov 3, 1999 1:00 am
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>Awww, you should have just posted the decode code. Hehe.

Never too late, good idea.
Admittedly my AMOS skills are a bit rusty with the Amiga still
in storage back in PA, but I think this routine will decode it:

Dim POSITION, CHAR$, SOURCESTRING$, STRINGCHAR$

SOURCESTRING$ = "IVWT?56_`a9`NZd\R@WYbeeF\iIqhM`LMgjvt/"
STRINGCHAR$ = ""

For POSITION = 1 To Len( SOURCESTRING$ )
CHAR$ = Mid$( SOURCESTRING$, POSITION, 1 )
CHAR$ = Chr$( Asc (CHAR$) - POSITION )
STRINGCHAR$ = STRINGCHAR$ + CHAR$
Next POSITION

Print STRINGCHAR$

sound sampler

Thu Nov 4, 1999 12:30 pm
<BURFIELD@simonburfield.co.uk>

@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #4388 of 8282

Re: sound sampler

Thu Nov 4, 1999 1:28 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


> Please could any one give me a code so i can use my sound sampler
> with amos. I have a techno sound 2 sampler and can not work out the
> code. I was think of using it for voice active stuff thanks.
> I saw a ghost.

Hello there!
I had a Techno Sound Sampler 2 for my Amiga at one time.
Yep, ordered the darn thing and when it arrived I discovered it would
not plug into the port in the back of my Amiga. Really sucked.
The damn plug was too small compared to the hole and the local
Radio Shack had no adaptor that would work. :(
Ah, but we are not here to discuss my problem, besides that was
years ago. lol!

So.... if I actually had such a thing hooked up to a computer I reckon
that by writing an extremely tight loop to grab values from the port, I
would be able to create a sound "image" (reproduction).

I imagine AMOS has its own commands to open and read from a port
but I would skip that and use a direct Peek (or perhaps Deek
depending on the width of the data being received) of the port address.

Sound sampling, like any realtime sampling, is pretty simple.
You basically just monitor the incoming data stream, pull values out as
fast as you can and store them linearly at another location.
The challenge is in the speed (frequency) of your sampling.
The faster you can grab a value and store it, the more samples you grab
within a certain period and time and the closer your sound "image" will
be to the original.

At a very basic level, the process could be as simple as:

Dim STORAGE

Reserve As Chip Work 11, 128*1024

For STORAGE = Start(11) To Start(11) + ( 128 * 1024 ) - 1
Poke STORAGE, Peek( PORTADDRESS )
Next STORAGE

What port are you plugging that thing into?

Anyway, I hope this helps ya. Tell us the port you are plugging that
thing into and someone can probably give you the hardware address
to monitor.

Happy sampling. :-)

--
       Manta Soft  -  Amiga programing & web page designing
          http://mantasoft.aio.co.uk/       ICQ: 21829166
 Homepage updated 5/8/99 --- James Bond on GFX Card & CPU players!
  - ------------------- Quote of the day: -------------------- -
In an atomic war, all men will be cremated equal

' Sampler by Andrew Crowe
' andrewcrowe@enterprise.net
'
'
Screen Open 0,320,256,2,Lowres


Poke $BFE301,0 : Rem Set input port
Poke $BFD200,6 : Rem Ini l&r channels
Poke $BFD000,2 : Rem Select left channel (4 for right)

Reserve As Chip Data 5,100000
S=Start(5)


Print "Calibrating..."

For DELAY=0 To 10000
Timer=0
For A=0 To 5525
Poke S+A,Peek($BFE101)-128
For D=0 To DELAY
Next
Next
If Timer=>25
Exit
End If
Print At(1,1);DELAY
Next



Cls
Print At(0,0);"Press any key to start Sampling..."

Repeat
For X=0 To 319
Plot X,Peek($BFE101)+8,1
Next
Wait Vbl : Wait Vbl
Ink 0
Bar 0,8 To 320,255
Until Inkey$<>""



Print "sampling..."

For A=0 To 99999
Poke S+A,Peek($BFE101)-128
For D=0 To DELAY
Next
Next



Print "Finished, press any key to play"
Wait Key
Sam Raw %1111,S,A,11050

	Message #4402 of 8283

Re: Data Statements

Fri Nov 5, 1999 2:09 am
Steve Eaborn <eaborn@powernet.co.uk>



>
> Yes, the majority of the variables are arrays. I did toy around with
> the idea of using memory banks to store and read my data but found it a
> very long winded way to go about it.
>

As I had a few moments (and a touch of insomnia 8) I thought I would put
this to the test, and found it's really not that bad (IMO).

It's probably a bit late now, but I thought I would post my efforts anyway
in case anyone's interested (anyway, it's a bit too quiet on this list for
my liking :( )

It does make use of peek$ & poke$, so you'll need amospro (or use a
procedure or something instead).


'****************************************************************
'storing strings/integers in databanks instead of data statements
'****************************************************************

'data to store
Data "This",91,5
Data "is",1025,211
Data "a",2147483647,0
Data "Test!",-22,-1

'define our arrays used to load the databanks
Dim A$(3),B(3,1)

STRINGLEN=0
NUMBERLEN=0

'read the data
For I=0 To 3

Read A$(I)
A$(I)=A$(I)+Chr$(0) : Rem append with null
Add STRINGLEN,Len(A$(I))

Read B(I,0),B(I,1)
Add NUMBERLEN,(2*4) : Rem 2 numbers @ 4 bytes each

Next I

'reserve some space in data banks, enough to store all the
'strings and numbers.
STRINGBANK=10
NUMBERBANK=11
Reserve As Data STRINGBANK,STRINGLEN
Reserve As Data NUMBERBANK,NUMBERLEN

'load the data into the databanks.
OFFSET=0
For I=0 To 3

'store string data
Poke$ Start(STRINGBANK)+OFFSET,A$(I)
'increment offset
Add OFFSET,Len(A$(I))

'store numbers (2 × 4 bytes each)
Loke Start(NUMBERBANK)+I*(2*4),B(I,0)
Loke Start(NUMBERBANK)+I*(2*4)+4,B(I,1)

Next I

'****************************************************************
'Everything up to this point can be removed in the final program once run.
'Then you can just leave the loaded databanks in the compiled program, or
'save them and load them in at run-time.
'****************************************************************

STRINGSTART=Start(10)
NUMBERSTART=Start(11)

'define different arrays this time, to test
Dim ST$(3),NU(3,1)

'reloading the number array is really quick and easy...
Poke$ Varptr(NU(0,0)),Peek$(NUMBERSTART,Length(11))

'reloading the string array is a bit more involved...
OFFSET=0
For I=0 To 3

'load the string
ST$(I)=Peek$(STRINGSTART+OFFSET,,Chr$(0))
'increment the offset
Add OFFSET,Len(ST$(I))+1

Next I

'finally, print it all out to prove it works
For I=0 To 3

Print ST$(I)
Print NU(I,0),NU(I,1)

Next I

' Sampler by Andrew Crowe
' andrewcrowe@enterprise.net

Screen Open 0,320,256,2,Lowres


Poke $BFE301,0 : Rem Set input port
Poke $BFD200,6 : Rem Ini l&r channels
Poke $BFD000,2 : Rem Select left channel (4 for right)

Reserve As Chip Data 5,100000
S=Start(5)


Print "Calibrating..."

For DELAY=0 To 10000
Timer=0
For A=0 To 5525
Poke S+A,Peek($BFE101)-128
For D=0 To DELAY
Next
Next
If Timer=>25
Exit
End If
Print At(1,1);DELAY
Next



Cls
Print At(0,0);"Press any key to start Sampling..."

Repeat
For X=0 To 319
Plot X,Peek($BFE101)+8,1
Next
Wait Vbl : Wait Vbl
Ink 0
Bar 0,8 To 320,255
Until Inkey$<>""



Print "sampling..."

For A=0 To 99999
Poke S+A,Peek($BFE101)-128
For D=0 To DELAY
Next
Next

Wait Key

	Message #4412 of 8283

Re: Re: sound sampler

Fri Nov 5, 1999 2:55 pm
Claude Heiland-allen <claude.heiland-allen@lincoln.oxford.ac.uk>


> From: "GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>
>
> > Please could any one give me a code so i can use my sound sampler
> > with amos. I have a techno sound 2 sampler and can not work out the
> > code. I was think of using it for voice active stuff thanks.
> > I saw a ghost.
>
> So.... if I actually had such a thing hooked up to a computer I reckon
> that by writing an extremely tight loop to grab values from the port, I
> would be able to create a sound "image" (reproduction).

Not too tight, unless you think that sampling at 1 MHz is a good idea...
The sampler probably wouldn't be able to react that quickly to the signal
anyway, and the parallel port isn't that good is it?

> I imagine AMOS has its own commands to open and read from a port
> but I would skip that and use a direct Peek (or perhaps Deek
> depending on the width of the data being received) of the port address.

Seems logical, would be getting bytes.

> Sound sampling, like any realtime sampling, is pretty simple.
> You basically just monitor the incoming data stream, pull values out as
> fast as you can and store them linearly at another location.

Not as fast as you can - you need to do it fast for high quality, but it is
more important to have a steady speed (otherwise you get frequency distortion).

> The challenge is in the speed (frequency) of your sampling.
> The faster you can grab a value and store it, the more samples you grab
> within a certain period and time and the closer your sound "image" will
> be to the original.

Yep. 44.1 kHz is CD standard, 22.05 kHz is a good compromise, 16 kHz is useful
for general samples for music modules etc, speech is intelligible down to about
4 kHz (8kHz you can recognize different voices).


Claude

	Message #4415 of 8283

Re: sound sampler

Fri Nov 5, 1999 5:03 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>Not too tight, unless you think that sampling at 1 MHz is a good idea...
>The sampler probably wouldn't be able to react that quickly to the signal
>anyway, and the parallel port isn't that good is it?
>Not as fast as you can - you need to do it fast for high quality, but it is
>more important to have a steady speed (otherwise you get frequency
>distortion).

Sampling at 1 MHz?? I would like to see somone hit that in AMOS!!
Hahahahaha. Granted I had a 20 MHz 68020 so I am not sure
what a 50MHz 68060 is capable of but I am sure AMOS is not going
to hit 1MHz sampling rates on anything.... not that they would be
needed. Who in hell would need that kind of dataflow? Even in the
sampling we do for custom manufacturing environments, several thousand
samples per second is efficient. I am sure even the missile guidance
systems are operating within a similiar range.
Audio recognition/reproduction is one of the most demanding forms
of real time sampling.

The speed should not fluctuate, obviously a tiny amount in a multitaskng
environment but that should be the least of your worries.
If you are using AMOS you had better make a lean and mean, supertight
loop in order to come anywhere close to grabbing the quantity of samples
per second to result in a quality recording.
Certainly, do not add any intentional delays between the sampling!!!


>Yep. 44.1 kHz is CD standard, 22.05 kHz is a good compromise, 16 kHz is
>useful for general samples for music modules etc, speech is intelligible
>down to about 4 kHz (8kHz you can recognize different voices).

Yes.... and 12K is very nice overall.
That is 12,000 samples per second.
That means you need to pull 240 samples/PAL Vbl, 200 samples/NTSC Vbl.
The 16K would require 320 samples/PAL Vbl, 267 samples/NTSC Vbl.

As with you, I am not sure what the Amiga parallel port can handle in
terms of data transfer. I know it can handle scanning devices as I had a
handheld scanner which transmitted a lot of data very quickly.
The exact bandwidth I do not remember.

If you were writing this in C or Assembler then you could think about
delays and tweaking everything for perfection but using AMOS your first
priority is gonna be on speed. Make the loop as tight(=fast) as
possible.
Then, after you have achieved the sampling rates you are after, it is
time to focus on the smoothing, processing tasks.

Have a super day!!! :-)

	Message #4421 of 8283

Re: sound sampler

Sun Nov 7, 1999 5:44 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>You can generate sin and cos waves through simple recurrence
>formulae (like y(n+1) = a * y(n) + b * y(n-1), you just need
>a and b... I have code somewhere too)
>Realtime drawing - do you mean like an oscilloscope monitor?
>I have no idea how to do this.

Should be pretty easy to make a functional oscilloscope in AMOS,
right? I mean all you need is a data stream to monitor.

Simply sample the data at the "in" port and then plot it on the screen
or connect the points from each frame to produce a better graph.

A simple oscilloscope could just (assuming a 640 pixel wide screen)
repeat this sequence....
Clear the screen
Sample data for 640 frames and plot the values on the screen

Happy sampling.

Re: Rotating a map

Sun Nov 7, 1999 11:14 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>couple years ago there was discussion about fast way of rotating
>map in 90 degrees. Has anyone got that code anymore?
>I'm too lazy and busy to go through all posted messages -archives on
aminet:)

Yes, I remember answering that question with a design of the process
involved and also the code.
Another guy then posted a follow-up to my message which had the code a
bit more
streamlined ( something I always like to see!! ).

Anyway, here we go:

If you have this map:

BDF
HJK
NPQ

And you rotated it clockwise 90 degrees, you would end up with:

NHB
PJD
QKF

As you can see.... all we are doing is remapping from horizontal to
vertical or
vice-versa, depending on how you are looking at it.

Basically, I see it as we are simply starting with the left column and
using that
as the source, we are starting with the top row and using that as the
destination.
Now we loop from left to right copying each column into the rows
(traveling from
top to bottom).

That is the whole theory in a nutshell.

I have no time as I am heading to a wrestling bash tonight and need to
leave
right now or I would post some code.

Happy rotating!!

	Message #4427 of 8283

Re: Re: Rotating a map

Mon Nov 8, 1999 5:57 pm
Claude Heiland-allen <claude.heiland-allen@lincoln.oxford.ac.uk>


> How is the fastest way of rotating 2d points?
>
> Let me put it another way:
> Lets say you have two (or more) points on the screen,
> and you want to rotate it lets say 30deegrees (by origo)?


x' = x * cos(angle) + y * sin(angle)
y' = x * -sin(angle) + y * cos(angle)


for lots of points store c = cos(angle) and s = sin(angle)


make sure you specify whether you are using degrees or radians
(default) - radians are quicker (degrees are converted to radians
before each calculation anyway)


if speed is crucial use lookup tables (as always...)


Claude

	Message #4429 of 8283

Re: Rotating a map

Tue Nov 9, 1999 1:08 am
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>When we are talking about the rotating world...
>How is the fastest way of rotating 2d points?
>Let me put it another way:
>Lets say you have two (or more) points on the screen,
>and you want to rotate it lets say 30deegrees (by origo)?


The fastest way of rotating a 2d point?

Hmm.... not sure. Let us all find out together.


Thanks to our good friend Claude for supplying the basic
formulas for rotation (which I would need to look up):
newxpos = oldxpos * cos(angle) + oldypos * sin(angle)
newypos = oldxpos * -sin(angle) + oldypos * cos(angle)

Okay, first thing we need to do is kill these cos(angle) and
sin(angle) tables.
We can create QCOS() and QSIN() precalculated data tables
(also known as Lookup Tables years ago, as Claude mentioned).

Just run a loop through the full range of rotation and
store the result of the Cos and Sin functions inside the data tables.
Dim QCOS#(360), QSIN#(360)
For ANGLE=0 To 359
QCOS#(ANGLE) = Cos(ANGLE)
QSIN#(ANGLE) = Sin(ANGLE)
Next ANGLE

Cannot quite remember how Amos defines floating point vars.
Might be #QCOS instead of QCOS# but at any rate you have AMOS
handsy so can find that out within a few seconds.

However, we are gonna kill that floating point nonsense anyway.
I have never found a need for floating point.
Integer math is much faster and can do anything floating point can.

Here is the integer version of the lookup tables:
Dim QCOS(360), QSIN(360)
For ANGLE=0 To 359
QCOS(ANGLE) = Cos(ANGLE) Asl 7
QSIN(ANGLE) = Sin(ANGLE) Asl 7
Next ANGLE

I am hoping that Asl is the AMOS version of the Assembler instruction
Asl Arithemetic Shift Left. Which is the fastest way to multiply by a
power of two. The result of the Cos and Sin functions is likely to be
something with a couple decimal places so ya can promote such a
number to a pure decimal by multiply it by 100.
Multiply is quite slow so instead we use Asl 7 which multiplies by 128
and is close enough to work perfectly anyway.

At this point the formulas for the rotation look like:
newxpos = (oldxpos * QCOS(angle) ) + ( oldypos * QSIN(angle) )
newypos = (oldxpos * -QSIN(angle) ) + (oldypos * QCOS(angle) )


Oh yeah we need to Shift back to the right by 7 to bring the value back
within the correct range too.

Also, those multiplies are gonna drain speed.... so someone else needs
to continue this quest to find the ultimate speed as I am leaving now.

Monday night wrestling is coming on soon and I still need to grab the
beer and pizza.


Good luck!!

Re: Re: Rotating a map

Tue Nov 9, 1999 8:51 am
"floquet" <floquet@hp-sc.univ-lille2.fr>




Truls Osmundsen wrote:
>
> From: Truls Osmundsen <ozzy1@online.no>

> * Svar til:* /GarfieldAtWork/ (#garfield@dtgrp.com#)
> * Dato var:* /08-Nov-99/
> * Emne var:* /[amos-list] Re: Rotating a map/
>
> When we are talking about the rotating world...
>
> How is the fastest way of rotating 2d points?
>
> Let me put it another way:
> Lets say you have two (or more) points on the screen,
> and you want to rotate it lets say 30deegrees (by origo)?
>
> Hope to hear from you!


It depends, in fact if you rotate points more often than you translate
them.
If rotation is the main thing, consider polar coordinates instead of
cartesian.
cartesian are : X pos, Y pos
polar are : Distance from center, Angle

Your display will be something like:
XD=XC+D(I)*Sin(A(I))
YD=YC+D(I)*Cos(A(I))

So if you want to rotate points just change all A(I) values and
everything will rotate.
If you want to woom-in zoom-out, just change all D(I) values...
If you want to translate ALL points, just change the center of screen
(XC and YC, i.e 320 and 100 for a 640x200 screen).
If you want to translate just some points, it's a little bit harder.

Hope this helps.

	Message #4431 of 8283

Re: Rotating a map

Tue Nov 9, 1999 2:23 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


ME> Here is the integer version of the lookup tables:
ME> Dim QCOS(360), QSIN(360)
ME> For ANGLE=0 To 359
ME> QCOS(ANGLE) = Cos(ANGLE) Asl 7
ME> QSIN(ANGLE) = Sin(ANGLE) Asl 7
ME> Next ANGLE
ME> At this point the formulas for the rotation look like:
ME> newxpos = (oldxpos * QCOS(angle) ) + ( oldypos * QSIN(angle) )
ME> newypos = (oldxpos * -QSIN(angle) ) + (oldypos * QCOS(angle) )

ME> ....someone else needs to continue this quest....

Wow, cool. Hey, I will see if I can contribute anything to this. :)

Hmm.... those multiplies need to go.
As always, ya need to look for patterns.
We have:
oldxpos * QCOS(angle)
and
oldypos * QCOS(angle)
both of which translate to:
somenumber * QCOS(angle)

What if we could expand on our earlier datatables and produce an
array which when fed with value, angle would return the newvalue?
Something like the following would then become possible:
NEWXPOS = POSBYCOS(OLDXPOS, ANGLE)
NEWYPOS = POSBYCOS(OLDYPOS, ANGLE)

Depending on how efficient AMOS deals with 2d arrays (obviously there
is multiplication involved internally to locate a cell within a 2d
array), this may provide no speed increase or a great speed increase.

Assuming the speed increase is significant we still need to consider the
table size.

The definition for ROTPOS is as follows:
POSBYCOS( 0....319, 0....359 ) lowres 320 pixel wide display.

This means we need 320 * 360 = 115,200 elements.
AMOS uses four bytes for each of these array elements, so total memory
required is 115,200 * 4 = 460,800 or 450k

We would also want to produce a table to update QSIN.
POSBYSIN( 0....318, 0....359 )

At this point, the rotation formulas are:
NEWXPOS = POSBYCOS(OLDXPOS, ANGLE) + POSBYSIN(OLDYPOS, ANGLE)
NEWYPOS = POSBYSIN(OLDXPOS, ANGLE) + POSBYCOS(OLDYPOS, ANGLE)


Let us discuss trade-offs.
We are looking at 900k for these two tables.
900k is a lot of RAM if you are using a 1MB machine so this is obviously
not workable. However, 900k is completely acceptable if the tables do
actually speed up the position calculations significantly.
One could say, hey, it is almost 2000. Get with the times, get some more
RAM. With a 4MB or higher machine 900k on these kind of data tables
is no problem.

However, you can also save some RAM by altering the table definitions.
Can you put up with rotation in 2 degree steps?
If you can then you have just saved 450k as the new table defs are:
POSBYCOS( 0....319, 0....179 ) and POSBYSIN( 0....319, 0....179 )
Just remember to use 0-179 in your system for rotation and all will be
fine.

If you can get by with rotation in four degree steps then you can drop
the RAM requirements even further, saving another 225k.
POSBYCOS( 0....319, 0....89 ) and POSBYSIN( 0....319, 0....89 )
Now, you would need to use 0-89 in your system for one complete rotation.
Still, 90 frames for one rotation is quite smooth!!
Both tables would now require 225k total.... workable even on a 1MB
machine.

It is time for me to get some actual work done, so I am sending this now.
Hope it provides some help.

We need to combine all of this stuff into an actual system at some point
but that will have to wait for another time or another person. :-)

Have a great day!!

	Message #4435 of 8283

Re: Rotating a map

Tue Nov 9, 1999 8:33 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


ME> NEWXPOS = POSBYCOS(OLDXPOS, ANGLE) + POSBYSIN(OLDYPOS, ANGLE)
ME> NEWYPOS = POSBYSIN(OLDXPOS, ANGLE) + POSBYCOS(OLDYPOS, ANGLE)
ME> POSBYCOS( 0....319, 0....89 ) and POSBYSIN( 0....319, 0....89 )
ME> Now, you would need to use 0-89 in your system for one complete
ME> rotation.
ME> Still, 90 frames for one rotation is quite smooth!!
ME> Both tables would now require 225k total....

One thing we also know is that we do not need the four bytes AMOS uses
for its variables. By focusing on this we can save memory and increase
speed.

By storing a 16-bit value instead of a 32-bit value for each element in
the POSBYXXX data tables, we can cut the memory requirements in half
again.

320 positions X 90 angles =
28,800 elements of data X 2 bytes each =
57,600 bytes
which is slightly over 56k.
Both tables will easily fit inside 113k.
Dim POSBYCOS, POSBYSIN
Reserve As Work 11, 57600 * 2
POSBYCOS = Start(11) : POSBYSIN = Start(11) + 57600

At this point, we would access en element using this formula:
VALUE = Deek( DPOSBYCOS + ( OLDXPOS * 180) + (ANGLE * 2) )

Two multiplies are in this formula so obviously we are not gonna use
that.

Now, we just saved a load of RAM.... 112.5K to be exact.
We can significantly increase the speed of the access to these
data tables if we are willing to sacrifice some of that RAM.

In the above formula, the ( OLDXPOS * 180) is finding the base address
of the Angles for each Position (90 possible angles X 2 bytes each).

If we were willing to throw away 76 bytes per Position (320 possible)
we would be losing only 24k.
We are now saying that we have 256 bytes of data for each of the 320
positions.
In reality, the last 76 bytes of each are unused (of course, you can
use them for something else if you need to).

The new formula for accessing the data table is:
VALUE = Deek( POSBYCOS + ( OLDXPOS * 256) + (ANGLE * 2) )

AHA!! Look at that 256 and 2. Both are values at a power of two!!!!
This means we can now completely eliminate all multiplication from our
forumulas and use something like this:
VALUE = Deek( POSBYCOS + ( OLDXPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )
VALUE = Deek( POSBYSIN + ( OLDXPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )

Again, I cannot remember the exact syntax of the AMOS Asl command but
I think you can see I we are shifting the value of OLDXPOS by 8 and
shifting the value of ANGLE by 1, in effect multiplying by 256 and 2
respectively.

I would dare say this new formula would be much faster than AMOS's
normal 2d array access.

Now, the full rotation formulas are:
XTC = Deek( POSBYCOS + ( OLDXPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )
YTS = Deek( POSBYSIN + ( OLDYPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )
NEWXPOS = XTC + YTS
XTS = -Deek( POSBYSIN + ( OLDXOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )
YTC = Deek( POSBYCOS + ( OLDYPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )
NEWYPOS = XTS + YTC

I broke that all down to better illustrate how we are using the new
data tables but in practice you can eliminate the four intermediate
variable loading steps and simply load the result of the full formula
directly into
NEWXPOS and NEWYPOS:
NEWXPOS = Deek( POSBYCOS + ( OLDXPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) ) +
Deek( POSBYSIN + ( OLDYPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )
NEWYPOS = -Deek( POSBYSIN + ( OLDXPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) ) +
Deek( POSBYCOS + ( OLDYPOS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )

Compare that to the original forumulas:
newxpos = (oldxpos * Cos(angle) ) + ( oldypos * Sin(angle) )
newypos = (oldxpos * -Sin(angle) ) + (oldypos * Cos(angle) )

Of course, there might be a mistake in there someplace and I cannot
test this stuff at the moment, but assuming it is reasonably accurate
(which I think is safe to say) we have completely eliminated the four
multiplications and floating point math.
We now have very detailed, and highly simplified forumulas for
producing the new rotated positions.

Another benefit of breaking everything down like this is that it
allows us to easly convert the formulas to Assembler which of
course gives you the maximum speed.

Another great thing is that you can easily test this right now and see
if the new pure integer, bit-shifting forumulas are faster than the
original floating point, multiplying formulas.

I would be interested in testing this myself if I had my Amiga handy.
Again, I am pulling this all from the top of my head "on the fly" so
there is no way I can test this and guarantee it is perfect.
All I can say is that is SHOULD be. Very damn close at the very
least!

DIM POS, ANGLE, TIME1, TIME2
Dim POSBYCOS, POSBYSIN

Reserve As Work 11, 57600 * 2
POSBYCOS = Start(11)
POSBYSIN = Start(11) + 57600

Timer=0
For POS=0 To 319
For ANGLE=0 To 89
NEWXPOS = (POS * Cos(ANGLE) ) + ( POS * Sin(ANGLE) )
NEWYPOS = (POS * -Sin(ANGLE) ) + (POS * Cos(ANGLE) )
Next ANGLE
Next POS
TIME1=Timer

Timer=0
For POS=0 To 319
For ANGLE=0 To 89
NEWXPOS = Deek( POSBYCOS + ( POS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) ) +
Deek( POSBYSIN + ( POS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )
NEWYPOS = -Deek( POSBYSIN + ( POS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) ) +
Deek( POSBYCOS + ( POS Asl 8) + (ANGLE Asl 1) )
Next ANGLE
Next POS
TIME2=Timer

Print "TIME1 = " + str$(TIME1)
Print "TIME2 = "+ str$(TIME2)

If all goes as planned, TIME2 will be much smaller than TIME1.



Good luck!!!!!!!

	Message #4437 of 8283

Re: Amos to C converter (fwd)

Wed Nov 10, 1999 12:46 am
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>> I`ve been thinking about making an Amos source code to C source code
>> converter so that I can recompile all my Amos stuff on the PC...
>As far as I can just figure out you will have a lot of problems in
> converting the very strange Amos-handling of data to c....
> How will you handle i.e. data statements, labels and accesories (IMHO
> the only cool things in Amos)...?


Hmm.... seems I missed this one until now. :-)

You could created a set of procedures and it should not be too bad....

int SetDataBuffer( unsigned int SIZEOFDATABUFFER );
Allocates space for the Data
Implementation.... just use calloc/malloc
Set the DataBuffer Base address to the start of the memory.
Initialize (unsigned int)DataReadPointer to 0
Initialize (unsigned int)DataWritePointer to 0

void Restore( char *DATALABEL );
Sets the DataBuffer base-offset to the location pointed to
by DATALABEL
Search the DATALABEL list, if the name is found then
Set the internal DataReadPointer equal to the associated
DATALABEL DataBuffer offset.

void Read( char* STRINGVARIABLENAME );
Reads the next item of data into STRINGVARIABLENAME
Implementation.... data is pulled from memory starting at
DataBuffer Base + DataReadPointer, as the data is pulled
in, the DataReadPointer is incremented. This continues until
the special dataitem termination characters are read.

void LabelData( char *DATALABEL );
Adds a label reference to the beginning of a section of data
Implementation.... Store the DATALABEL in a list along with
the current value held in DataWritePointer

void Data( char *DATASTRING );
Adds dataitems to the databuffer.
Implementation.... DATASTRING is parsed, dataitems are
seperated by a single comma (",").
As each dataitem is located it is inserted into the DataBuffer
where each dataitem will be terminated with some character
combination we choose.
As each dataitem is added to the DataBuffer the DataWritePointer
is updated ( incremented by length of DataItem + terminators ).

Which in practice could be used like this:
int dataitemnumber;
char dataitem[80];

if ( SetDataBuffer( 5 * 1024) ) {
LabelData( "DATAONE" );
Data( "This is a string, 5, That was a number." );

Restore( "DATAONE" );
for ( dataitemnumber=0; dataitemnumber < 3; dataitemnumber++ ) {
Read( dataitem );
printf( "%s\n", dataitem );
}

}
===========

Granted it is not as straight-forward as AMOS/BASIC data statements
but considering I just threw this simple design together in ten
minutes, I am sure if someone actually focused on this problem for
a few days they could come up with an excellent solution.

May your data always be free of corruption.


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #4438 of 8283

RE: [Amos-list] Re: Rotating a map

Wed Nov 10, 1999 8:15 am
Simon Burfield <Burfield@simonburfield.co.uk>


Thanks for helping me on that 3D room code!


From: "GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>

ME> Here is the integer version of the lookup tables:
ME> Dim QCOS(360), QSIN(360)
ME> For ANGLE=0 To 359
ME> QCOS(ANGLE) = Cos(ANGLE) Asl 7
ME> QSIN(ANGLE) = Sin(ANGLE) Asl 7
ME> Next ANGLE
ME> At this point the formulas for the rotation look like:
ME> newxpos = (oldxpos * QCOS(angle) ) + ( oldypos * QSIN(angle) )
ME> newypos = (oldxpos * -QSIN(angle) ) + (oldypos * QCOS(angle) )

ME> ....someone else needs to continue this quest....

Wow, cool. Hey, I will see if I can contribute anything to this. :)

Hmm.... those multiplies need to go.
As always, ya need to look for patterns.
We have:
oldxpos * QCOS(angle)
and
oldypos * QCOS(angle)
both of which translate to:
somenumber * QCOS(angle)

What if we could expand on our earlier datatables and produce an
array which when fed with value, angle would return the newvalue?
Something like the following would then become possible:
NEWXPOS = POSBYCOS(OLDXPOS, ANGLE)
NEWYPOS = POSBYCOS(OLDYPOS, ANGLE)

Depending on how efficient AMOS deals with 2d arrays (obviously there
is multiplication involved internally to locate a cell within a 2d
array), this may provide no speed increase or a great speed increase.

Assuming the speed increase is significant we still need to consider the
table size.

The definition for ROTPOS is as follows:
POSBYCOS( 0....319, 0....359 ) lowres 320 pixel wide display.

This means we need 320 * 360 = 115,200 elements.
AMOS uses four bytes for each of these array elements, so total memory
required is 115,200 * 4 = 460,800 or 450k

We would also want to produce a table to update QSIN.
POSBYSIN( 0....318, 0....359 )

At this point, the rotation formulas are:
NEWXPOS = POSBYCOS(OLDXPOS, ANGLE) + POSBYSIN(OLDYPOS, ANGLE)
NEWYPOS = POSBYSIN(OLDXPOS, ANGLE) + POSBYCOS(OLDYPOS, ANGLE)


Let us discuss trade-offs.
We are looking at 900k for these two tables.
900k is a lot of RAM if you are using a 1MB machine so this is obviously
not workable. However, 900k is completely acceptable if the tables do
actually speed up the position calculations significantly.
One could say, hey, it is almost 2000. Get with the times, get some more
RAM. With a 4MB or higher machine 900k on these kind of data tables
is no problem.

However, you can also save some RAM by altering the table definitions.
Can you put up with rotation in 2 degree steps?
If you can then you have just saved 450k as the new table defs are:
POSBYCOS( 0....319, 0....179 ) and POSBYSIN( 0....319, 0....179 )
Just remember to use 0-179 in your system for rotation and all will be
fine.

If you can get by with rotation in four degree steps then you can drop
the RAM requirements even further, saving another 225k.
POSBYCOS( 0....319, 0....89 ) and POSBYSIN( 0....319, 0....89 )
Now, you would need to use 0-89 in your system for one complete rotation.
Still, 90 frames for one rotation is quite smooth!!
Both tables would now require 225k total.... workable even on a 1MB
machine.

It is time for me to get some actual work done, so I am sending this now.
Hope it provides some help.

We need to combine all of this stuff into an actual system at some point
but that will have to wait for another time or another person. :-)

Have a great day!!

Official AMOS WWW: http://members.xoom.com/AmosFactory/front.html

Re: Re: Amos to C converter (fwd)

Thu Nov 11, 1999 5:42 am
"Rune Zedeler"<rune@zedeler.dk>


Garf wrote:

> int SetDataBuffer( unsigned int SIZEOFDATABUFFER );

> void Restore( char *DATALABEL );

> void Read( char* STRINGVARIABLENAME );

> void LabelData( char *DATALABEL );

> void Data( char *DATASTRING );

Well, yeah, that way you could implement "simple" data statements and labels
to them.
(Uh,oh, long time no C... Damn, It's all fuzzy to me...)

But we still need the "goto" and "gosub" labels...
(Don't say that procs can be used instead. That's not always the case. I.e.
if you have to refer to a label in the main program then it's not a good
idea to be located in a proc):
And... As I said - only simple use is supported in your (I know, quick)
c-implementation.
I.e. you can goto/gosub an expression, like this:

Do
G$=Inkey$
Trap Gosub "LABEL_"+G$
Loop
LABEL_A: Print "you tammed the A-key" : Return
LABEL_1: Print "One for the money,"
LABEL_2: Print "Two for the show,"
LABEL_3: Print "Three to get ready now, go cat go..." : Return

etc...
(Well, I find this a brilliant replacement for the missing "Switch" statement,
and it actually works...!)

In AMOS it is also actually legal to put any expression (not just simple
types) in data statements:

Restore _PATH
_PATH$=""
While not Exist(_PATH$+_FILE$)
read _PATH$
Wend
Open In 1,PATH$+_FILE$
..
_PATH:
Data "S:"
Data "C:"
Data "Work:AMOS/files/"
Data Fsel$("Can't locate file, please specify dir!","(Do NOT select the file)")


(yeah, a fileselector in a data statement. Everytime the thing is read, a
fileselector pops up :) )

(Off course, this was typed on an O2 at the university, probably with loadz
of typoz)

-Rune Zedeler, rune@zedeler@dk

PROJECT LEADER
One day, a project leader was asked to submit a review of one of his
employees.
He wrote the following:
01. Bob Smith, my assistant programmer, can always be found
02. hard at work in his cubicle. Bob works independently, without
03. wasting company time talking to colleagues. Bob never
04. thinks twice about assisting fellow employees, and he always
05. finishes given assignments on time. Often, Bob takes extended
06. measures to complete his work, sometimes skipping coffee
07. breaks. Bob is a dedicated individual who has absolutely no
08. vanity in spite of his high accomplishments and profound
09. knowledge in his field. I firmly believe that Bob can be
10. classed as a high caliber employee, the type which cannot be
11. dispensed with. Consequently, I duly recommend that Bob be
12. promoted to executive management, and a proposal will be
13. executed as soon as possible.
Regards - Project Leader

Shortly thereafter, the HR department received the following memo from the
project leader:
Sorry, but that idiot was reading over my shoulder while I wrote the
report sent to you earlier today. Kindly read only the odd numbered lines
for the true assessment of him.
Regards - Project Leader

AMOS Next Generation

Thu Nov 11, 1999 9:39 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


Ya know.... if people really wanted a Next Generation AMOS....
it should not be that difficult to create.

Obviously, it would take time to implement the thousand commands
found in AMOS Pro + the most popular extensions but a basic, usable
version could be created in reasonably short period of time.

If such a thing were created, I think it should be platform independant
and renamed to something like NGB: The 21st Century BASIC.

When you really think about it, taken a command at a time, each task
is pretty damn simple.

Using C or C++ the code would be almost fully portable if created the
right way (ie. all audio/video operations channeled through a seperate,
platform specific, audio/video library(ies).

Since these libraries already exist for every platform out there.... well,
I am sure you can see the point.

Anyway, it is kind of exciting to think about such a project, in fact I
think Keith (aka Braneloc) should get started on this right away.
Hahahahaha. :)

Just a thought.

	Message #4445 of 8283

AMOS Next Generation - update

Thu Nov 11, 1999 10:34 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>Using C or C++ the code would be almost fully portable if created the
>right way (ie. all audio/video operations channeled through a seperate,
>platform specific, audio/video library(ies).

Of course, what I mean is we pass them through one central
library which will initially contain skeleton code and not do much of
anything.

However, each audio/video function can be implemented by using
libraries found each platform.

For example:
PlotPixel( int Bitmap, int xpos, int ypos, int color)
Is what we call from the main program code when the programmer is
wanting to plot a pixel.
On the Amiga, PlotPixel may in turn call the GMS PixelPlot routine,
on the PC it may call DirectX or WinAllegro pixelplot, etc.

Yes, it would place another layer between command and actual
implementation but it would not make that much difference and the
ease of portability would be well worth it.

Besides, this will make Keith's job easier! lol.

NGB: 21st Century Basic - DOES ANYONE WANT IT?

Hello all.

Well, Keith and I have been talking about this project.

We were wondering if there is really anyone interested in a new
language similiar to AMOS but upgraded.

The main idea is that this language will be completely platform
independant. If your program works on the AMIGA it will work
on the PC and MAC with no changes at all.

In order to accmplish this task we will use a simple bitmap
graphics and raw sound format. Do not worry, compression will
be an option or perhaps standard!!

It will also use a custom audio-video library which pipes everything
out to the individual platform audio-video libraries currently avalable.
I have already mentioned this in a previous post.

The thing is.... is anyone interested in using such a language?????


If you give a hoot about this please say so!!

	Message #4455 of 8283

NGB: 21st Century Basic - DOES ANYONE WANT IT?

Sat Nov 13, 1999 7:41 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


EH>Will it have 2 and a half D software bobs (bobs that rotate and scale)?

No problem.... we can stick that stuff in.
I would not take it serious if it did not have these kinds of things!


EH>And a good 2D modeler, and maper?

Not sure what you mean by a 2d modeler and mapper?


>Will it have true 3D, and a good 3D modeler, and maper?

It can have these things.... if we find a good library which already
has these features. :-)
That is the beauty of this design. We are creating a core language
which can tap into all of the best C/Asm libraries floating around
out there.

Worse case scenario is that I dig out my 3d game programming
book and consult with Adam Parrot. In other words we make our
own super fast 3d lib in C.


>Will it have software multi-transparent screens ((screens that let sub
>screens show through color 0 (color 0 is transparent or noncolor black
>would need to be another number))?

On the PC this would be easy..... simply because things like WinAllegro
support this and we only need to call their functions.

Some of these things are just not possible on a standard Amiga.
Sure we could code it in, hell we can make anything but the problem
is how can we possibly dynamically update an entire bitmap fast
enough for realtime framerates? I will give it my best shot but unless
you have a graphics card you will be looking at AGA dual playfield
mode which gives you 6 + 16 colors in each screen.


>Will it support all screen modes, and colors modes ((2, 256, 1.6 million)
>(320x200, 640x480, 1024x576 etc...)?

It will support all of the modes you have mentioned, at least not color
depths.

We are planning on offering the following:
SCREEN MODE 0: 320 x 200 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 1: 320 x 200 x 16 bit color
SCREEN MODE 2: 640 x 400 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 3: 640 x 400 x 16 bit color
SCREEN MODE 4: 640 x 480 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 5: 640 x 480 x 16 bit color
SCREEN MODE 6: 800 x 600 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 7: 800 x 600 x 16 bit color
SCREEN MODE 8: 1024 x 768 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 9: 1024 x 768 x 16 bit color
EXTENDED MODES:
SCREEN MODE 10: 320 x 200 x 32 colors
SCREEN MODE 11: 320 x 200 x 64 colors
SCREEN MODE 12: 640 x 400 x 32 colors
SCREEN MODE 13: 640 x 400 x 64 colors
SCREEN MODE 14: 640 x 480 x 32 colors
SCREEN MODE 15: 640 x 480 x 64 colors

Obviously, the extended modes are really only of value to Amiga
programmers and on the PC and MAC these will be mapped to
8-bit color displays.

Basically, the whole system is you ask for one of these screen modes
and you get the closest thing available on the other platforms.
To you, it is seamless and does not effect anything.


All of these things can be implemented in time.... if you are asking if
everything you have mentioned will be available within two months the
answer is no. However, given time all things are possible and even
likely.

People should know my main concern is always on FAST, COMPACT
code. It is what I do best. Keith and I have already discussed the
basic design which would offer the maximum speed while
allowing us to create incredibly compact executables.

BTW- Name change from Keith, now called BNG....
BASIC: the Next Generation
.... I assume. :-)

BNG: Thanks for your support.

Sat Nov 13, 1999 8:50 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


RK> I use AMOS because it is easy to use and pretty powerful.
RK> If you can make me a language that is as easy to use, has more
RK> power and even is platform-independent, will I use it?
RK> YES! I'll even pay for it :)

Thanks for the vote of support!
There is no doubt that Keith and I CAN do it, the question is WILL
we do it?? Hahahahaha.
The more people that are honestly interested in such a project
and the more Keith hears of money will certainly push BNG one
step closer to reality. :-)


CK> An upgraded AMOS. I think that's a good idea. :)
CK> I am <interested>.
CK> This would be a great thing!
CK> I wish I knew enough to help you guys!

Thanks for your vote of support!!
There is no doubt that Keith and I CAN do it, the question is WILL
we do it?? Man, I feel like I am having Deja Vu. Hahahaha. ;)

If we decide to do this project.... you can help in one of three ways.
ONE: $$$ motivate Keith. I can ask him to work on the project for
the fun and challenge of it and he may contribute some time.
You can send keith $5(or pounds) and he will contribute time.
Hmm.... how many people are on this list? Hahahahaha.
TWO: Research. You can perform resource availability research.
THREE: Testing and feedback.
FOUR: Example programs. You can create some of the BNG example
programs which would come "packaged" with the language.

Please note that IF we do this project and you want to contribute
Testing&feedback or writing example programs, we may require you
to send a letter of intent which simply states you will not send the
stuff out to anyone else without our approval.
Ultimately, I have no problem with sharing the information but we
would not want the project being spread around in bits and pieces
the whole time we are working on it.

Well, I think we have enough interest at this point to go ahead and
start on a simple prototype. From what we had discussed, Keith
will be handling the parsing and I will handle the code generation.

Obviously, we will not be implementing anything major at this time.
Just a test of some of the concepts we have thrown around.
I would say we will end up with a simple compiler which can handle
integer variables, for.... next loops, maybe the ability to add
variables/values, and I guess we would need to stick in some type
of print command.

That should be enough to test some concepts, solidify a development
strategy and of course the best part is that we will have proof of the
compact, speed code we are convinced our design will produce.

I will talk to Keith about this and ideally we have something working
no later than tomorrow. It's gonna be FAST!! Hahahahaha. :-)

Create_Full_Screen(640,480,8); // Opens a screen 640x480 8bit 256 colours

whats more, if i called it again with different parameters, it would change
the screen automatically. Its great for game coding, once you create the
procedures.

have to learn it. With power, there is always going to be millions more
options, parameters etc. It won't be BASIC like it is now, it will be a
close form of C, especially for it to be portable.

lot of them like in AMOS right now, imagine the slow-down you'll get,
mainly because everything in an option would be turned on, rather than
specifying bits you wanted. It would result in thousands of lines of
repeated code, just to change a simple parameter, if you worked around it
with procedures.

I say the way to go, is tyo create a massive collection of
graphics/sound/video structures in C, that way, anyone can download and use
them.

	Message #4482 of 8283

Other updated AMOS projects and their effect on BNG

Sun Nov 14, 1999 7:41 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>> We were wondering if there is really anyone interested in a new
>> language similiar to AMOS but upgraded.
>> The main idea is that this language will be completely platform
>> independant. If your program works on the AMIGA it will work
>> on the PC and MAC with no changes at all.
>Sorry, but I must have missed something: isn't that what the Amos
>Development Group was supposed to be working on?

Who? Amos Development Group?? Oh, you mean Keith and I.
Hahahaha. We are currently dabbling with the idea of developing
a powerful new BASIC programming language similiar to AMOS,
however BNG would not be a simple upgraded AMOS, rather we hope
to create a language as exciting now as AMOS was when it first
came out.


>Yes, I would be interested in it, but I'm afraid I would not be of
>much help, as I know no programming language except Amos.
>You could base it on Java, and thus get help from Pietro...

No problem. I am not sure of the connection between Pietro and Java
but as I have mentioned in a previous post.... BNG does indeed
borrow from the JAVA model. :-)
Whether there is another language being developed or not is really
no concern to us. Personally, I have my doubts as these things have
been announced several times on this and I have never seen any
actual files, test results, etc. Keith and I have a combined amount
of 40 years of programming experience during which time we have
both created our own languages, compilers, parsers, etc.
The difference with BNG is that if we decide their is enough interest
and we choose to commit to the project.... it will be done.
If another group do actually produce an upgraded AMOS that is
great as it simply means you will have more options to choose from.

	Message #4485 of 8283

Re: NGB: 21st Century Basic - DOES ANYONE WANT IT?

Sun Nov 14, 1999 7:14 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>I have a small question in the middle of all this enthousiasm:)
>Won't this new language be a "powerful amos for pc" with very crappy amiga
>port?

It will be a new BASIC type of language. We are obviously, modeling it
after all of the stuff we liked about AMOS while also copying the best
features of other languages to get away from the weaknesses of AMOS.

The language is being developed in parallel on the PC and Amiga at the
moment. Since yesterday, we have a working compiled example program
(very simple: around 8 commands have been implemented at this time)
which is fast as hell and incredibly small (193 bytes).


>It seems to me like most of the things you're going to include and the
>speed they need to work at is coined for the PC (or other "brute force"
>and/or chunky gfx platforms)...

That is very true in a sense. Obviously, the more power you have
available on the main CPU the more capable any language becomes.
For the Amiga, BNG will allow you to everything that AMOS does and
then a bit more. It will also do it much faster and require much less
RAM.


>And hows is easy plane manipulation possible when it's heavily based in
>chunkyness or portability...

I will only say that a command or two or three can be stuck in for
anything like this. Remember, the whole system is that we are relying
on existing Audio/Video libraries. Gamesmith for example offers
manipulation of the bitplanes. GMS is another option.


>And why are there no PAL modes in the plans? It's fine that 200 and
>scanlines are most "portable" to vga-type systems, but do you want people
>to have a 56 line black border under their monitors or do you assume all
>amiga users live in the us?

I did not include PAL modes because I am an NTSC user, living in the US.
Hahahaha!! :)

Sure we can add these to the Extended modes section.
On the PC, they will be mapped to ModeX displays or more likely centered
in a standard NTSC size display which means you would lose the border.
Hmm.... or possibly, I can scale them in realtime.

We obviously have not had time to test every single thing.
We had a concept.
We created a design.
We implemented a test of the design.
It works.

Anything like the points you have mentioned can be handled. I am not
worried about these issues at all. There are always options such as the
three I have already thought of the PAL to PC display mapping.

is interested in seeing the current example code execute on a PC.
It is a simple nested loop three levels deep, adding vars together and
incrementing another variable and displaying the values on the screen for
the duration of the loops. The compiled code is 193 bytes in size.
It is about 95% the speed of optimized C code. It is FAST!!
As soon as Keith installs the C kit on his Amiga or I get a decent cross
compilation system installed (working on it just takes time and it has
been a busy weekend.... replying to these emails, hahahaha) we will
have the Amiga version ready to test. Actutally, I think Keith may have
an emulator working but it would be much slower than the real thing.

	Message #4491 of 8283 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

AMOSPro, AmoNG & BNG :)

Sun Nov 14, 1999 10:13 pm
Pietro Ghizzoni <ghizzo@agonet.it>


Hi!

Ok... since there are some intersting posting around the list, is time to
reply :)

First some infos about the new AMOSPro distribution... it's called AMOSPro
Phoenix, and it's structure is ready. Now the whole AMOS system is hold in
only one directory.. no more libs and config files around your HD... i've
removed
where possible the craps in the code and deleted all the unuseful stuff.

As stated i've not worked on the original sources since it's not very
usefull.. they are a mere pile of shit... the upgrade is represented by our
new extensions and all the features added.... they replace most of the AMOS
stuffs with the equivalent OS friendly result. Don't worry.. same design...
same style... easy as always. Before someone ask... no Intuition/AGA Bobs at the
moment...
first i need to create a full RTG system, then i will be able to quickly
add the Bobs support.

Finally now i've a serious system with PPC board and Gfx Card so i can
develop a more compatible kernel for my extension.

I'm again working on the GUI Extension... Rev. Giark is working on the
docs... essentially this is the only missing part of the project.... but
it's the more important. Probably i'll release soon my second project..
it's called AmiGate, and it's the first AMOSPro Phoenix project. You'll
have a idea of the new features like localization, app windows and appicons,
fast
internet connection (i've totally rewrote the old system) and a totally OS
integration.When?

AmiGate in 2 weeks.... AMOSPro Phoenix 25 December :) (Rev. Giark??)

Probably a lot of peoples doesn't belive any more in my work, and i can
understand..... i'm sorry but the time is the main problem, and i'm the
only one working on this project.

Now few words about the AmosNG project... Brice Fromentin is the author,
but he is vanished in the limbo with all the project.

I don't know the BNG design, but i can give you a idea of the AmosNG one.

Since the main goal is the portability, the AmosNG compiler works like a
C++ compiler, but in a higher way :)

For those who doesn't know how a C compiler works:

the C compiler translate your C source into ASM source, and after using a
internal or
external assembler the executable will be created from the ASM sources.

The AmosNG compiler translate your code into C++ code and after using
automatically the GNU C++ or EGGS compiler the executable will be
created. Since the GNU C++ compiler is available (for FREE) on ALL the
platforms, you can port your programs on ALL the OS of this world.

The extesions are simple C linkable libraries.....

I really hope that the BNG project became a reality... but i'm worried
about some things.... the language is interpreted or compiled?

If compiled, what kind of debugger can we use? And what about the PC and
Amiga CPU code generation?

At the moment the bobs, directX, 3D blah, blah, blah are NOT important!
First we need a working compiler able to clue together the basic statements
of the language like For/Next, If EndIF, A=(5*B)+4-Z and so on.

Keith... if you are really able to do it (able to do it means also to have
the *time* to do it!!) well... good luck! No time for coding, but i will be
very happy to help you in the desgin of the language.

A portable AMOS-like language is the only reasonable solution for the
future... i'm working with Java and i've some AMOS<->Java ideas....


---


Bye!

>Will it have true 3D, and a good 3D modeler, and maper?

It can have these things.... if we find a good library which already
has these features. :-)
That is the beauty of this design. We are creating a core language
which can tap into all of the best C/Asm libraries floating around
out there.

Worse case scenario is that I dig out my 3d game programming
book and consult with Adam Parrot. In other words we make our
own super fast 3d lib in C.


>Will it have software multi-transparent screens ((screens that let sub
>screens show through color 0 (color 0 is transparent or noncolor black
>would need to be another number))?

On the PC this would be easy..... simply because things like WinAllegro
support this and we only need to call their functions.

Some of these things are just not possible on a standard Amiga.
Sure we could code it in, hell we can make anything but the problem
is how can we possibly dynamically update an entire bitmap fast
enough for realtime framerates? I will give it my best shot but unless
you have a graphics card you will be looking at AGA dual playfield
mode which gives you 6 + 16 colors in each screen.


>Will it support all screen modes, and colors modes ((2, 256, 1.6 million)
>(320x200, 640x480, 1024x576 etc...)?

It will support all of the modes you have mentioned, at least not color
depths.

We are planning on offering the following:
SCREEN MODE 0: 320 x 200 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 1: 320 x 200 x 16 bit color
SCREEN MODE 2: 640 x 400 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 3: 640 x 400 x 16 bit color
SCREEN MODE 4: 640 x 480 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 5: 640 x 480 x 16 bit color
SCREEN MODE 6: 800 x 600 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 7: 800 x 600 x 16 bit color
SCREEN MODE 8: 1024 x 768 x 8 bit color
SCREEN MODE 9: 1024 x 768 x 16 bit color
EXTENDED MODES:
SCREEN MODE 10: 320 x 200 x 32 colors
SCREEN MODE 11: 320 x 200 x 64 colors
SCREEN MODE 12: 640 x 400 x 32 colors
SCREEN MODE 13: 640 x 400 x 64 colors
SCREEN MODE 14: 640 x 480 x 32 colors
SCREEN MODE 15: 640 x 480 x 64 colors

Obviously, the extended modes are really only of value to Amiga
programmers and on the PC and MAC these will be mapped to
8-bit color displays.

Basically, the whole system is you ask for one of these screen modes
and you get the closest thing available on the other platforms.
To you, it is seamless and does not effect anything.


All of these things can be implemented in time.... if you are asking if
everything you have mentioned will be available within two months the
answer is no. However, given time all things are possible and even
likely.

People should know my main concern is always on FAST, COMPACT
code. It is what I do best. Keith and I have already discussed the
basic design which would offer the maximum speed while
allowing us to create incredibly compact executables.

BTW- Name change from Keith, now called BNG....
BASIC: the Next Generation
.... I assume. :-)

Official AMOS WWW: http://members.xoom.com/AmosFactory/front.html

>Now few words about the AmosNG project... Brice Fromentin is the author,
>but he is vanished in the limbo with all the project.

That is so damn strange. Why these people do this I will never
understand. Drop the project if you feel the time requirements are too
much for you.... that I can understand but to take all the source,
eliminating any progress which was made, makes no sense.
If we decide to commit to the creation of BNG and I decide that the
project is no longer fun, the moon turns red or I feel it is draining too
much time.... I will pass everything on to Keith.... well, actually Keith
will have everything anyway as we have been sending updates back
and forth every day now.


>I don't know the BNG design....
>I really hope that the BNG project became a reality... but i'm worried
>about some things.... the language is interpreted or compiled?
>If compiled, what kind of debugger can we use? And what about the PC and
>Amiga CPU code generation?

The BNG design is exactly this:
First, it is all a concept which became a design and then was tested.
It works, is blazingly fast and incredibly compact.
At least for me, BNG is still an idea.... something which I know can
be created but I have not commited to doing so at this time. I am
simply experimenting at the moment. I am not sure of where Keith
stands on this decision.

The language takes advantage of the fact that there are powerful
audio and video (ie. game programming) libraries avalable for the
Amiga, PC, MAC and probably every other platform out there.
The language is being written in straight C.

Having written BASIC to machine code compilers in the past, we
have decided to try another approach this time. As you know,
many compilers compiled to a sort of SpeedCode, something
about one step or two above machine code.
Obviously, SpeedCode is not a set format and any author can
create their own version.

In this way, BNG will be similiar to Java which produces ByteCode.

The SpeedCode principle allows BNG to be easily ported to
every platform out there as long as we can compile the C source
into the engine executable.

It also opens up some very interesting abilities such as multi-tasking
programs or interrupt driven routines. These things are very easy to
implement when you are using a Virtual CPU.

The language design is basically being thrown together by both Keith
and I "on the fly" at the moment (dabbling).
The compiler is being created by Keith on the
Amiga.
The BNG Virtual Machine (CPU) is being created by myself on the PC.


>A portable AMOS-like language is the only reasonable solution for the
>future... i'm working with Java and i've some AMOS<->Java ideas....

Definitely.... agreed. :)

	Message #4523 of 8283

Re: Re: BNG - multitasking capabilities

Tue Nov 16, 1999 12:18 pm
Claude Heiland-allen <claude.heiland-allen@lincoln.oxford.ac.uk>


> >I really really hate hard-coded limits, especially when there is no need.
>
> I see no need for the need.

eh?

> >> (Integer)NumMessagesWating = CHECKMESSAGES(Integer)TaskNumber
> >So you'll be busy-waiting too. It just gets better and better...
>
> Busy waiting for what???
> You call the routine... if it says 0 then you have nothing talking to
> you. If you want to wait until something actually sends you a message
> then you can, but it would make more sense to continue processing.

Say you have a task, that does processing when it gets a message. Then
once it has finished processing it replies (or whatever). The task now
has nothing to do until the next message arrives. You really need a
WaitMessage() function, because otherwise the task has to loop, checking
for messages, which wastes CPU time. Imagine 30 tasks (about average on
my system - dos handlers, workbench, various utils) all frantically looping
just checking for messages.

Better to have the sendmessage function check if the destination is waiting,
and if it is then wake it up. Like exec.library does ;)


Claude


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #4524 of 8283

Re: Re: BNG - multitasking capabilities

Tue Nov 16, 1999 12:19 pm
Claude Heiland-allen <claude.heiland-allen@lincoln.oxford.ac.uk>


> Just to be on the extra safe side, I will set it at 32 tasks.

Why have any limit?


Claude


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #4525 of 8283

Re: Re: BNG - multitasking capabilities

Tue Nov 16, 1999 12:24 pm
Claude Heiland-allen <claude.heiland-allen@lincoln.oxford.ac.uk>


> I don't see the point of the tasks having a direct line of communication if
> you use global variables you can send a flag to remote trigger actions. You
> are implementing Amiga DOS type global variables right?

Using global variables is unsafe - you need semaphores to regulate access
otherwise unpredictable results and deadlocks can occur. Basically the
problem is that a task switch could occur between reading the variable
and writing it. Example:

x = 2

task 1 reads x
task 2 reads x
task 1 writes x = x+1
task 2 writes x = x+1

result x = 3, although it should be 4.


Concurrency needs to be handled very carefully.


Claude


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #4526 of 8283

BNG - THE PROJECT THAT MIGHT BE....

Tue Nov 16, 1999 2:21 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>> Is their a web page for this project? I'd like to see a command summary.
>Hmm, Garfield, do you think a we should do a command summary and
>website after barely 2 days development, or should we wait till the end
>of the week?

Hahahahaha!! I guess I need to stop replying to posts and
getting things fired up, huh?

Just so everyone knows.... there is no official BNG project at this
time. We are just dabbling, messing around and having fun.
There is no command summary, no website, no anything yet.
Everything comes into existence about ten minutes before it is
implemented.

At work I do enough "proper" development, creating design docs,
cost analysis's, etc so this is very refreshing to just jump in and
have fun with this thing in a sort of crazy fashion.

I know people are gonna say that is no way to approach this kind
of project.... but I think it is. As long as we do not take this
thing too seriously and just have fun with it, progress will continue
at the current rate.

I think a main reason why we have seen so many attempts at
creating a new language fail is that everyone gets into so much
detail, the progress slows to a crawl then stops completely as
people become buried in a ton of design issues, pressure to make
everyone happy (impossible), etc.

Personally, all I wanted to know was that people were interested in
a new language. Now, I am just gonna continue consulting with
Keith and just having fun with this project. This is just a "use what
we already know" kind of thing which is why development will be
at a tremendous rate as long as we keep things straight-forward
and fun!! :)

@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #4528 of 8283

Re: BNG - Multitasking and Task Communication

Tue Nov 16, 1999 2:22 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>> Busy waiting for what???
>> You call the routine... if it says 0 then you have nothing talking to
>> you. If you want to wait until something actually sends you a message
>> then you can, but it would make more sense to continue processing.

>Say you have a task, that does processing when it gets a message. Then
>once it has finished processing it replies (or whatever). The task now
>has nothing to do until the next message arrives. You really need a
>WaitMessage() function, because otherwise the task has to loop, checking
>for messages, which wastes CPU time. Imagine 30 tasks (about average on
>my system - dos handlers, workbench, various utils) all frantically
>looping just checking for messages.
>Better to have the sendmessage function check if the destination is
>waiting, and if it is then wake it up. Like exec.library does ;)

Of course, gotcha!! See, I always checked for incoming events and
if there were some, processed them, if not then did other things
(scrolling messages, loading data, etc.) unless it was just a simple
application where everything was completely Event oriented.

I had thought about this over the weekend and to be honest even
though event driven languages are very cool in their own way
(Oracle, VB, etc), I am leaning toward the more linear style of
processing offered by AMOS and C.

However, you make a valid point, and I can see where this would
be very handy when dealing with the multtasking processing....so
we now give two choices:
CHECKMESSAGES immediately returns the number of messages in
the message buffer allowing you to continue processing.
WAITFORMESSAGE freezes the task until a message arrives.

	Message #4529 of 8283

Re: BNG - Multitasking capabilities

Tue Nov 16, 1999 2:23 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>>Just to be on the extra safe side, I will set it at 32 tasks.
>Why have any limit?

Mainly because this has just been completely "in fun".
Keith and I have been operating under this rule for the
three days of development: SIMPLICITY AND FUN!

So, we have one limit in BNG. The language will "only"
be able to execute 32 independant user-written programs.
I just do not see where this is any major restriction.

We are not building a multitasking operating system or
an operating system at all for that matter (well, okay maybe
a super scaled down one in a sense but hardly anything like
Intuition), rather a language. If someone wants unlimited tasks
they can run BNG multiple times on the Amiga or PC.

	Message #4530 of 8283

Re: BNG - multitasking, OS or language

Tue Nov 16, 1999 2:51 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>I don't see the point of the tasks having a direct line of communication if
>you use global variables you can send a flag to remote trigger actions. You
>are implementing Amiga DOS type global variables right?

No, we are not implementing Amiga DOS type global variables.
We are not copying the Amiga operating system at all.
We simply want BNG to be able to handle 32 independant tasks.

I came up with those commands for direct communication just because
they seemed sensible and obvious. A task needs to be able to send
messages, check for new messages, and receive messages. Of course,
we now have a fourth command which will wait until a message arrives.

That is probably as close to the Amiga OS as BNG will get.
We just think it would be cool to allow these tasks to have direct
communication. Less overhead, easy to process, yet very powerful.

Remember, ideas are simply popping into our minds all the time.
Just this moment I was thinking of getting a cup of coffee.... er, I mean
I was thinking of event driven stuff that we do need in BNG and of
course a menuing system and dialog boxes would be two things we
will need to implement through an Event Driven System.

	Message #4533 of 8283

Speed....

Tue Nov 16, 1999 7:34 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


As you know I have been saying BNG is gonna be fast.
In most other language comparisons (say AMOS - BLITZ)
that translates to a 50% increase in overall performance.

Great news.... I did some timing tests this morning at home and
the BNG code is now hitting an incredible 99% of the speed
of C code.
This means that even after we have added the overhead of
messaging, multitask tracking, and whatever else may creep
in the days ahead, BNG should still deliver 90-95% of the speed
of C!!!!
For those who are interested.... Keith and I performed some
tests last year and found that C was by far the fastest of any
Amiga languages except pure Asm (obviously).

We compiled a test program in AMOS, BLITZ, BLITZ+Asm, and C.
The speed was in the order I just listed (slow to fastest) with the C
program being five times faster than the AMOS version.

Does this mean BNG will allow you to make games with 5x as
much stuff on the screen at the same frame-rate as your current
AMOS version? Of course not.... but it is reasonably safe to
assume the completed Amiga version of BNG would deliver
2-4x the speed of AMOS, depending on how graphic intensive
the program is.

BTW - this is a lunchbreak message!! Hahahahaha. ;)

	Message #4535 of 8283 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Re: BNG - multitasking capabilities

Wed Nov 17, 1999 6:58 am
Eric Hyland <a007193t@bc.seflin.org>


On Tue, 16 Nov 1999, Claude Heiland-allen wrote:

> From: Claude Heiland-allen <claude.heiland-allen@lincoln.oxford.ac.uk>
>
> > I don't see the point of the tasks having a direct line of communication if
> > you use global variables you can send a flag to remote trigger actions. You
> > are implementing Amiga DOS type global variables right?
>
> Using global variables is unsafe - you need semaphores to regulate access
> otherwise unpredictable results and deadlocks can occur. Basically the
> problem is that a task switch could occur between reading the variable
> and writing it. Example:
>
> x = 2
>
> task 1 reads x
> task 2 reads x
> task 1 writes x = x+1
> task 2 writes x = x+1
>
> result x = 3, although it should be 4.
>
>
> Concurrency needs to be handled very carefully.
>
>
> Claude

Rem f1=0 readable f1=1 nonreadable

x = 2: f1=0

if f1=0 then let task read x
Let f1=1 : task 1 reads x

if f1=0 then let task read x
task 2 waits to reads x

task 1 writes x = x+1: Let f1=0

if f1=0 then let task read x
Let f1=1 : task 2 reads x
task 2 writes x = x+1: Let f1=0

result x = 4, it should be 4 all's ok.

Tasks have priorities so the CPU only works on one instruction at a time, so
this should work. I like global variables for global things, and local
variables for local things. Basic lets me program how I want to right or
wrong it's up to me I hate structured programing languages. Please include
global variables, so I can continue to be as unstructured as I want to be.

Eric Hyland
a007193t@bc.seflin.org
