	Message #4549 of 8283

Re: BNG - Task Communication

Thu Nov 18, 1999 2:40 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>Global variables would be in the system but they would be
>local to the individual task. You would use the messaging system
>to communicate directly with any tasks as needed.
>>....if I have 4 tasks that need to use the same variable I would
>>have to make 4 variables that contain the same information
>>(wasting memory), and setup 4 variable updating routines that
>>inform all 4 programs to update (needlessly wasting cpu cycles).
>>This does not seem very resource thrifty.

Yes, that is a correct analysis of the basic usage.
The idea is to offer encapsulation.... independant self-contained
tasks. In AMOS (C, etc) when a programmer calls a procedure,
any data passed into that procedure is stored in new variables.
This sort of thing is happening all the time throughout a program
seamlessly to the programmer.
As far as wasted CPU cycles are concerned.... whether you are
analyzing a local variable or a global variable is not going to make
any difference.
The only additional overhead I can see would be if you wanted
to inform the other three tasks ("simultaneously") that new data has
arrived. Using a Global variable, you would simply make one
statement, such as:
G_AllTasksUpdate = TRUE
instead of sending three messages from Task0 before it could
continue processing, such as:
SENDMESSAGE Task1, "NewData!!"
SENDMESSAGE Task2, "NewData!!"
SENDMESSAGE Task3, "NewData!!"

One way of handling this would be to simply create a chain:
Task0: SENDMESSAGE Task1, "NewData!!"
Task1: SENDMESSAGE Task2, "NewData!!"
Task2: SENDMESSAGE Task3, "NewData!!"

Another way would be for Keith & I to bit encode the TaskIDs
the same way AMOS handles Voice selection in the Sample commands:
Task0: SENDMESSAGE Task1+Task2+Task3, "NewData!!"

Regardless of the global variable issue, the bitvalue based TaskID
could be cool, however it would once again lock in a limit on the
number of tasks.
If we used 64-bit TaskIDs then obviously we could only have 64 unique
TaskIDs which means we could only have 64 tasks (which I think is
plenty but I know, I know.... BNG is supposed to be "unlimited").
Something to consider.... Keith, what do you think?



>If you like, I guess we could always stick in a few GlobalTaskVariables
>so you could set flags. :)
>> Do you mean have both Global, and Local variables ( A,A$,A%,
>>and @A,@A$,@A%)? Then yes that's what I would like.

Well, actually I meant just some Integer variables so you could
set flags and stuff. hahahaha.
What the heck, making some Globals are no problem, but I like
to organize things a bit.... so I am now thinking of predefined
instead of dynamic variables:
IGTV0 thru IGTV15 16 Integer Variables
FGTV0 thru FGTP15 16 Floating Point Variables
SGTV0 thru SGTV15 16 64-character String Variables
See, my mind keeps thinking of things like this because I am
thinking part of the fun in programming is working out how to work
around the limitations of the language. If we make a truly unlimited
language where would the fun be in figuring out a cool way to do
something?? (yeah, I am twisted, huh?) Hahahahahahahaha.

See, now that we have basically commited to doing this project these
are issues we are gonna actually look at and design. We wanted to
avoid that and build this "on the fly" but I guess we need to take a
day or two and actually properly design the language.... I suppose.
Just cannot have things becoming too serious.... life should be fun!!


@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@@

	Message #4550 of 8283

Re: Re: BNG - Task Communication

Thu Nov 18, 1999 1:54 pm
Claude Heiland-allen <claude.heiland-allen@lincoln.oxford.ac.uk>


> >Global variables would be in the system but they would be
> >local to the individual task. You would use the messaging system
> >to communicate directly with any tasks as needed.
> >>....if I have 4 tasks that need to use the same variable I would
> >>have to make 4 variables that contain the same information
> >>(wasting memory), and setup 4 variable updating routines that
> >>inform all 4 programs to update (needlessly wasting cpu cycles).
> >>This does not seem very resource thrifty.
>
> The only additional overhead I can see would be if you wanted
> to inform the other three tasks ("simultaneously") that new data has
> arrived. Using a Global variable, you would simply make one
> statement, such as:
> G_AllTasksUpdate = TRUE
> instead of sending three messages from Task0 before it could
> continue processing, such as:
> SENDMESSAGE Task1, "NewData!!"
> SENDMESSAGE Task2, "NewData!!"
> SENDMESSAGE Task3, "NewData!!"

Unsafe! Example: task 1 may be doing some calculations with a global
variable, task 2 changes it, so the calculation gets messed up. You
really do need semaphores - but you could get the compiler to hide the
gory details from the end user programmer.

Also, if you have one variable for "update all tasks", how do you know
when all the tasks have got the message? It would work the first time
you changed the variable, but after that it doesn't make sense (when do
you set the flag to false?). Use messages, maybe have a special send()
function that sends to all tasks but your own. Compare BOOPSI - that
has a class that sends messages sent to it to all the objects in a list,
with checking to make sure that each object gets each message exactly
once.

The general theme is: some clever people have worked out the theory of
multiple tasks, and the best ways to avoid problems. So obey the rules
of laziness:

1: there's no point doing something if someone has already done it
2: if something's worth doing, someone else will do it first if you
wait long enough, then see rule 1


Claude

	Message #4553 of 8283

BNG or NGB whatever that new language is called.

Sat Nov 20, 1999 12:09 am
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>Looks like something monsterous is going to happen (I mean that
>positively)!

Monsters?! Run, RUN EVERYONE.... AS FAST AS YOU CAN!!


>I'd like the language to be completely Stand-alone (initially), so that it
>doesn't have to rely on the myriad of GUI's that come and go...etc'.

The only things required (at this time) would be either an Amiga running
Workbench or a PC running Windows (preferably 95 or higher).

We are not using anything from any specific operating system because
A) it is completely unnecessary and B) it would obviously make porting
the language difficult. We can make streamlined routines which do
everything we need and run faster than the "take care of everything"
OS routines while still being completely portable.

The only thing that will be used on each platform which is specific to
that platform will be an audio/video library. However, these audio/video
routines will be seamlessly linked in so you will not have to do anything
other than the BASIC programming. Before someone screams about
program size... let me point about that a PC game demo I created with
Allegro and C is only 219k (uncompressed) even though it displays VGA
and SVGA graphics, plays custom sound samples and a few tunes.

	Message #4557 of 8283

New entry and OSdevKit

Sat Nov 20, 1999 5:48 pm
Marco Vettorello <marcoegon@tiscalinet.it>


Hi everybody on this list!
I'm a new entry. My name is Marco Vettorello, i'm Italian, 22 years old. I'm
studying as a psicologist at the University of Padua.
First: my English is far from being good, so have fun with my errors ;-)

I'm using Amos since 1990/1991 and I've a little of experience. I've written
some utilities in AmosPro using the Gui Extension and all the other extensions
made avaiable for free on the AmosFactory. In particular: Vocabo and MVslink

Vocabo is a spellchecker. It uses an Arexx port, waits until a word is sent to
it and then checks if it's a legal word of your language. For the moment i've
included only italian vocabulary but on my HD there's and archive with English
words. It's on Aminet. In the archive there are some Arexx script working with
BlacksEditor but I think it will simple to translate them for another TextEd

MVslink is a splitter. Have you got really big files? Do you want to transport
them with floppies? Then this utils is for you! It uses a smart memory usage
not Bload and Bsave but Sload and Ssave: it loads only a part of the big file
and save to disk, it loads the next freeing the previous allocated memory and so
on... Also in the archive on Aminet there SubSlink that enables you to slink a
file bit by bit: you can save the first 3 bytes on a particular file, the last
10 bytes on another file. It's usefull for deleting headers and footers in
datafile.

Ah, each archive has the source code! :-Ð

Also I've written a simple cripting util (MVcrypt) that uses a fast algorithm
known as St.Cyr
But it's not on Aminet. Ask me it if you have some interest. Source included.

A simple memory indicator. 2 gauge in a window on your wb screen. Source
included, ask me it.

A nice (mmmh.. maybe) address organizer using random access file. Source
included, ask me it.

I hope to give my hands to you and, of course, I need yours.
Amos can still do much for our community. That's the real goal.

My first question is about OSdevKit. There is a better documentation? A lot of
commands aren't documentated.

Bye.

Re: Golden Rule#1: Interactivity and Feedback

Sun Nov 21, 1999 5:30 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>Amos has not a good editor _at this time_.
>I would like to use a standard texted.
>I would like to have an Arexx port.
>And other features in order to have Amos as much as possible OS compliant.
>'I want to know _now_ what I'm doing'.

<sounds of scribbling on random scraps of paper>
Yes, I agree with your point on the interpreter. That is without a doubt
one of the main reasons AMOS is such a nice development system.
Whether you are playing a game, using a database or developing software
one thing remains constant: you need the ability to quickly and
seamlessly interact within the environment while receiving logical
feedback.

The interpreted nature of AMOS makes it ideal to develop in as you can
quickly change a line here or there, click Run and immediately see the
results of your changes. It is the aspect which makes AMOS such a fine
choice for new programmers.

Actually, if you are using something like GCC on the PC on decent
machine then you can have that too. My sources compile into executables
in seconds, but that is another story.

HAPPY THANKSGIVING, MY FELLOW AMERICANS!!
HAPPY THURSDAY, MY NON-AMERICAN FRIENDS!!

Great news.... Keith and I discussed this BNG project last night and
it looks like everything is well under control. We have actually spent
the past few days designing things and now have several designs
floating around for the different aspects of the project. These design
docs will almost certainly come in handy, we hope! hahahaha ;)

We are still targeting a pre-Christmas release of the demos (both
De/Compiler and VirtualCPU. You will most likely NOT be able to do
anything with audio or video other than simple text but you can still
have fun messing around with the foundation, comparing speed, and
even writing text-based dungeon romps, etc. (Ah, I remember those
days well.... amazing how excited you could get over confronting an O
or finding some T).

We might even release a source or two which you can compile and
actually execute. :-)

Give me a "b".... "B"
Give me an "n".... "N"
Give me a "g".... "G"
What do we have? "bng", "bng!", "BNG", "BNG!", "BNG!!", "BNG!!!"
We appreciate your support! hahahaha. :-)

Have a nice day!

AMOS Professional released as PD.

Fri Nov 26, 1999 2:26 am
"Adam Parrott" <parrottsoft@usa.net>


Hello, there.

For those who have been searching high and low for a copy of AMOS
Professional 2.0 and the Compiler: look no further. An Amiga site called
"Back to the Roots" (http://back2roots.emuunlim.com) has received
permission to post the entire AMOS library, from AMOS Classic to AMOS Pro,
.zip'ed in .ADF format (readable by UAE) on their site. You may obtain any
of the AMOS Basic library by visiting their Files area at:

http://back2roots.emuunlim.com/About/History/Files//211/

or, if you wish to read the news page about the release, goto:

http://back2roots.emuunlim.com/About/History/

and read up a brief history of AMOS and find some useful Amiga utilities. I
have yet to install these AMOS disks in WinUAE, but I assume that they will
work. The "AMOS Professional Update 2.0" seems to include the update to the
Pro Compiler as well, for those who are looking for the Compiler. :)

On a side note (CBATNAM-related): I await some new gfx routines from PAC.
As soon as I get them, then I will release the latest demo for the Dugeon.

And lastly, I wish everyone a Happy Thanksgiving. Thanks again and enjoy!

	Message #4583 of 8283 - ASCII Signiture Rebuilt

Re: Interrogating a website via AMOS

Fri Nov 26, 1999 5:02 pm
Andrew Crowe <andrewcrowe@enterprise.net>


Hi Everybody,

> Now that we have some TCP support for our beloved language, I was wondering if
> anyone could enlighten me as to how I may use it to interrogate a website
> that contains updating data (it's a weather site) so that I can ask it to
> chase up the updating weather data for me? Any ideas how I might start doing
> this? Or even how I might start experimenting?

This little program will download my homepage index page to ram:

change it how you need :)

See ya :)
--
       Manta Soft  -  Amiga programing & web page designing
          http://mantasoft.aio.co.uk/       ICQ: 21829166
 Homepage updated 5/8/99 --- James Bond on GFX Card & CPU players!
  - ------------------- Quote of the day: -------------------- -
All the leaves a brown, and the sky is grey,
California dreaming, on such a weary day.
-- Mamas&Papas.

HTTPDOWNLOAD["members.tripod.com/80","/~mantasoft/index.html","Ram:Index.html"]



Procedure HTTPDOWNLOAD[SERV$,URL$,FILE$]

E$=Chr$(13)+Chr$(10)
Reserve As Work 1066,8192

'Open the connection and destination file
'-------------------------------------------

AMINET=Tcp Open(1,SERV$) : DEST=Tcp F Open(2,FILE$,0)

If AMINET

SIG=Tcp Signal(1,0,0) : ADR=Tcp Address : Tcp Download ADR To 2
REQ=Tcp Send$(1,"GET "+URL$+E$,0) : Tcp Reset
'MSG["Done sending HTTP request; waiting for response.",0]

Do

W=Gui Event : PKT=Tcp Packet : TE=Tcp Error : TT=Tcp Total

If W=-9
If PKT=SIG

'Gui Set 1,1,0,TT : Gui Set 1,3,0,TT/Max(Tcp Time,1)
Exit If TE><0

End If
End If


Multi Wait

Loop

Else

A=Gui Req("Error!","Unable to open connection!","Ooopsss!")

End If

Tcp Close


End Proc

	Message #4592 of 8283

Re: Unrelated to BNG

Sat Nov 27, 1999 11:56 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>>For a version of BNG check out www.darkbasic.com
>>it is available and easy.
>>It is created by Lee Bamber a former member of Francois
>>Lionets Team with Europress.
>Unfortunately, this seems to be available only for the PC.
>.... expecting to charge at least $50.

I would actually hesitate to even call this a BASIC as it seems
more like a glorified (3D) game construction kit than a true
programming language but this is simply my impression.

Can it be used to create a database, utilities, etc?
I wonder if it can actually handle this(??):
For REP=1 To 10
Print REP * 10
Next REP

Actually, I am not even sure this so called Dark Basic can handle
non 3D rendered games(???).

Still, DB does look like a very cool development kit for anyone
interested in developing 3d rendered games for the PC.


I mainly just want to make sure people realize that Dark Basic,
although appearing to be a powerful 3D Game Creation System, is not
a version of BNG nor is it associated with BNG in any way.

BNG is a real programming language which is about 80-90% directly
compatible with AMOS while still being much faster than AMOS.
BNG will be available for both Amiga and PC at the same time which
means you can throw together a simple "demo" on the Amiga, compile it
and execute that demo on both the Amiga and the PC.

	Message #4599 of 8283

Re: Re: Darkbasic - peecee only - a tad off topic.

Sun Nov 28, 1999 9:20 am
"Keith Hill" <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


-----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----
Hash: SHA1

> > The only problem with it is the middle mouse button doesn't
> > scroll on the editor - and it quits every once in a while, save
> > proggies, and you're fine. There are some wierd quirks with the
> > language, but those can be programmed around easy enuf. Could
> > change screenmodes quicker, but then again, couldn't all top of
> > the range graphic cards.
> What's the code like though? Is it simmiler to AMOS? :)

Some of it is quite amos-like, some of it isn't. It is a full basic
system, works in an amos-like editor "interpreted" or compiled, I
seem to be having very little trouble testing it at the mo.

Most of the commands are "slightly different" but the conversion is
quite easy. Suggest you power up a second machine to look at the
.htm help files, as the amos-like context sensitive help is disabled
in this version. You don't NEED to though, the help clicks on/off
quite easily, similar to the way amos does it, except via html. In
other words, you can't type in amos listings without messing around a
bit.

It saves its proggie files (.dba) in raw text format, so you can mess
with them externally too.

Some of the commands are a bit stricter than amos, some commands
accept only integers instead of variables, and it took me a full 15
seconds to figure out while...wend is now while...endwhile.

In a couple of hours at the machine I should have a more interesting
test proggie available, probably with some 2D and 3D thrown in for
good measure, and doing something interesting.

They supply a basic test set of (probably) everything you need in the
initial download, and have additional stuff available online as well.
The demos and examples provided are quite reasonable.

You can read most of the code with little effort, as with anything
though, a hard copy manual might be helpful, as online help can get a
tad tedious. Then again, you can live without it.

The suprising thing is the power of the commands... it seems to be
acomplishing things a heck of a lot simpler than it should !
Comparing to amos 3D ? Well, it exceeds ALL the limits of amos 3D,
has support for landscapes, objects, animated objects, movable
objects, plenty of textures, FOG, and a bunch of other stuff I havn't
looked at yet.

	Message #4604 of 8283

BNG: The language that never was?

Mon Nov 29, 1999 3:29 pm
"GarfieldAtWork" <garfield@dtgrp.com>


>If BNG ever gets finished that is....
>(hopefully it will, but what happened to the last AmosNG?....)

Hahahahaha! Well, we only had the initial concept and started throwing
messages around on the list a mere two weeks ago.

Bearing in mind that Dark Basic was in development for over two years and
is still not 100% complete. How long has Paul Manias(?) been working on
the GMS library? Seems like it has been a few years now.

I am not criticizing these people for the length of development time,
rather I mention them to simply illustrate that it does take time to
produce a working language or library system. Also, we are not talking
about a simple project.... full multitasking built into the language
itself, fully portable between platforms, ability to run the same BNG
program on multiple platforms, 80%+ directly compatible with AMOS, etc.

It is almost certain that BNG would be in development for 3-4 years if
produced by the creators of Dark Basic or anyone else.

So, please keep in mind that BNG is a rather large project and if we are
able to actually complete it by Christmas 2000 that will be incredibly
fast in comparison to similiar projects (3-4 x faster)!!

We are both trying to devote 2-3 hours per week on this project but
sometimes that is very difficult to do. As long as BNG remains
interesting we will work on it. If we become bored with it then we will
throw up the source for what we have and someone else can carry it
forward.

In the latest news I devoted my time yesterday and created the core
file system. Keith is working on compiler/decompiler tweaks when
he is not playing with Dark Basic or building websites for his clients.

If you have seen the demo's you'l know the power it has. My favourites are
the seademo, and the little tank demo, virtually no code, yet a lot of
result =))

My tiles are 16-bit too =)) I could make it go even faster if I wanted too =))

> Instead of drawing directly to the screen, can't you draw to a hidden
> bitmap and the do a blitcopy all at once to the Video RAM?
> The way the PC architecture's Video Board access is designed a one time
> dump of a full bitmap should be much faster than several hundred small
> blits.
>

Thats pretty much what the sync commands do. In the start of your code,
you'd have like:

sync on : rem Manual control over screen drawing

function DoAllGfx
rem Do all the graphics, paste all tiles, update player scores, update
scroller, and anything else graphics related

...

sync
endfunction

the sync command on it's ownb them tells the system to do all the drawing,
instantly. Instead of drawing it, swapping to back buffer, bringing back
buffer to front etc. It will just draw everything in one jump. Many many
times faster =))

Right now, im working on a 3D racing game, and its looking very good =))
even for me, hehe

	Message #4619 of 8283

Re: Re: Darkbasic - peecee only - It is.... HUGE!!

Tue Nov 30, 1999 7:52 pm
"Keith Hill" <Braneloc@mirex.demon.co.uk>


-----BEGIN PGP SIGNED MESSAGE-----
Hash: SHA1

> I will definitely check into this thing.... what kind of code
> does it
> produce? The executable demos I downloaded were kind of bulky.

Kind of bulky...

> DB is freakin' HUGE!!

Yeah, it also likes bitmap and wav formats. I can live with that
till the upgrade fixes it. I could write my own conversion routines
I suppose.

> What makes DB better than any other development system, such
> as Euphoria(http://www.rapideuphoria.com/), for intance?

None of the tedious mucking about with darkbasic, it's all
integrated, and it uses my 3D graphics card and FFB joystick, does
real time textured polygons at stupidly complex levels way quick, 3D
animations, bobs, easy as falling off a log and a whole heck of a lot
of other stuff...

I seem to have collected 100megs of bitmaps for it already. I hate
bitmaps. I remember when that was a lot of space. Ah well, only
another 6.5 gigs left on my drive. I suppose I should empty the
couple of gigs in the trash sometime and delete a couple of CD
archives. Ah well...

> The zip for Euphoria is only 550k for Windows and 482k for Linux
> (yep, they already have multiplatform support).

True, Euphoria is a hell of a lot smaller, has faster download
mirrors, but going by the demos the things done in euphoria could
have been done in any language. Ok, I'll admit I've only
superficially glanced at euphoria, but after the same cursory glance
at darkbasic, there is no comparison. Tedious mucking about ? Been
there, done that... Darkbasic is all in one. Yeah, a couple of bits
need a bit of work, it has a few quirks I have found already, and
I'm already encroaching on its limits, but I can live with that and
program around it.

Why am I going on about it so much ? For a very long time, I have
been unsatisfied with every programming language I have tried, none
of them did everything I wanted. Blitz had a sucky editor and needed
too much messing about to get anything done, C++ or C was just pure
messing about, peecee basics were just unfriendly and nasty, visual
stuff just didn't feel right somehow, the miscellanous languages just
sucked for doing anything cool, amos didn't do AGA properly, and ran
too slowly for my liking, but in the long run was the best
development system I had encountered so far. I got all the
extensions for it, I even messed around writing my own 3D routines,
and got along quite well writing a brand new amos extension which got
tedious very quickly. There is only so much low level stuff you can
do without getting bogged down in the detail. The designs got so
powerful, the implementation would have taken forever. I have
written a lot of stuff in a lot of different languages, I'm the one
who broke all the records on my programming courses, and yet I have
been so restricted. I looked at that java thing that is supposed to
be the new amos but it didn't seem to be released yet. (Maybe its
out by now, I don't care anymore) I've looked at a lot of junk, and
seen a lot of promises. I'm sure the promises will all pay off in
the end, but it is taking so long, and I am really fed up of waiting.
Yeah, I can do a hell of a lot of really cool stuff with C, pointers
to functions and other stuff, but it takes so long to write anything
with it, its a million declarations and I just don't seem to have the
time for that any more.

Then a couple of days ago I saw darkbasic, and even the beta was
everything I have been looking for all this time. All of a sudden,
instead of being held back, I have my creativity back. I can now
actually go implement all those things I have been planning for years
without reinventing the wheel and getting tied up in quirks. I can
actually do REAL programming again.

Thanks Maurice, for pointing it out to me !
